class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#d02010; color:white;"> </span> 1,684–3,477</div></div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cerebrovascular_disease_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cerebrovascular_disease_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/220px-Cerebrovascular_disease_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cerebrovascular_disease_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/330px-Cerebrovascular_disease_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Cerebrovascular_disease_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/440px-Cerebrovascular_disease_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cerebrovascular_disease_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Disability-adjusted_life_year" title="Disability-adjusted life year">Disability-adjusted life year</a> for cerebral vascular disease per 100,000 inhabitants in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> <div> <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"> <tbody><tr> <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;"> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#b3b3b3; color:black;"> </span> no data</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffff65; color:black;"> </span> &lt;250</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#fff200; color:black;"> </span> 250–425</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffdc00; color:black;"> </span> 425–600</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffc600; color:black;"> </span> 600–775</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffb000; color:black;"> </span> 775–950</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff9a00; color:black;"> </span> 950–1125</div> </td> <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;"> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff8400; color:black;"> </span> 1125–1300</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff6e00; color:black;"> </span> 1300–1475</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff5800; color:black;"> </span> 1475–1650</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff4200; color:black;"> </span> 1650–1825</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff2c00; color:black;"> </span> 1825–2000</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#cb0000; color:white;"> </span> &gt;2000</div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div></div>
<p>Stroke was the second most frequent cause of death worldwide in 2011, accounting for 6.2 million deaths (~11% of the total).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_top_10_causes_of_death_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_top_10_causes_of_death-225">[225]</a></sup> Approximately 17 million people had a stroke in 2010 and 33 million people have previously had a stroke and were still alive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fei2013_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fei2013-18">[18]</a></sup> Between 1990 and 2010 the number of strokes decreased by approximately 10% in the developed world and increased by 10% in the developing world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fei2013_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-Fei2013-18">[18]</a></sup> Overall, two-thirds of strokes occurred in those over 65 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fei2013_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-Fei2013-18">[18]</a></sup> South Asians are at particularly high risk of stroke, accounting for 40% of global stroke deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indian_Stroke_Association_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-Indian_Stroke_Association-226">[226]</a></sup> Incidence of ischemic stroke is ten times more frequent than haemorrhagic stroke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup>
</p><p>It is ranked after heart disease and before cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Donnan2008_2-19"><a href="#cite_note-Donnan2008-2">[2]</a></sup>  In the United States stroke is a leading cause of disability, and recently declined from the third leading to the fourth leading cause of death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid21778445_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid21778445-228">[228]</a></sup> Geographic disparities in stroke incidence have been observed, including the existence of a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stroke_belt" title="Stroke belt">stroke belt</a>" in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">southeastern United States</a>, but causes of these disparities have not been explained.
</p><p>The risk of stroke <a href="/wiki/Exponential_growth" title="Exponential growth">increases exponentially</a> from 30 years of age, and the cause varies by age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ellekjaer1997_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-ellekjaer1997-229">[229]</a></sup> Advanced age is one of the most significant stroke risk factors. 95% of strokes occur in people age 45 and older, and two-thirds of strokes occur in those over the age of 65.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NINDS1999_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-NINDS1999-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Senelick1994_213-1"><a href="#cite_note-Senelick1994-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>A person's risk of dying if he or she does have a stroke also increases with age. However, stroke can occur at any age, including in childhood.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Family members may have a genetic tendency for stroke or share a lifestyle that contributes to stroke. Higher levels of <a href="/wiki/Von_Willebrand_factor" title="Von Willebrand factor">Von Willebrand factor</a> are more common amongst people who have had ischemic stroke for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> The results of this study found that the only significant genetic factor was the person's <a href="/wiki/Blood_type" title="Blood type">blood type</a>. Having had a stroke in the past greatly increases one's risk of future strokes.
</p><p>Men are 25% more likely to develop strokes than women,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NINDS1999_46-3"><a href="#cite_note-NINDS1999-46">[46]</a></sup> yet 60% of deaths from stroke occur in women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Villarosa1993_216-1"><a href="#cite_note-Villarosa1993-216">[216]</a></sup> Since women live longer, they are older on average when they have their strokes and thus more often killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NINDS1999_46-4"><a href="#cite_note-NINDS1999-46">[46]</a></sup> Some risk factors for stroke apply only to women. Primary among these are pregnancy, childbirth, <a href="/wiki/Menopause" title="Menopause">menopause</a>, and the treatment thereof (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hormone_replacement_therapy_(menopause)" title="Hormone replacement therapy (menopause)">HRT</a>).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hippocrates.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="710" data-file-width="483" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Hippocrates.jpg/170px-Hippocrates.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Hippocrates.jpg/255px-Hippocrates.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Hippocrates.jpg/340px-Hippocrates.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hippocrates.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a> first described the sudden paralysis that is often associated with stroke.</div></div></div>
<p>Episodes of stroke and familial stroke have been reported from the 2nd millennium BC onward in ancient Mesopotamia and Persia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a> (460 to 370 BC) was first to describe the phenomenon of sudden <a href="/wiki/Paralysis" title="Paralysis">paralysis</a> that is often associated with <a href="/wiki/Ischemia" title="Ischemia">ischemia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Apoplexy" title="Apoplexy">Apoplexy</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> word meaning "struck down with violence", first appeared in Hippocratic writings to describe this phenomenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stroke1996-Thompson_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stroke1996-Thompson-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merginet2001-Kopito_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merginet2001-Kopito-233">[233]</a></sup>
The word <i>stroke</i> was used as a synonym for apoplectic <a href="/wiki/Seizure" title="Seizure">seizure</a> as early as 1599,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> and is a fairly literal translation of the Greek term.  The term <i>apoplectic stroke</i> is an archaic, nonspecific term, for a cerebrovascular accident accompanied by haemorrhage or haemorrhagic stroke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> was described as having an <i>apoplectic stroke</i> that deprived him of his speech shortly before his death in 1546.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1658, in his <i>Apoplexia</i>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Jakob_Wepfer" title="Johann Jakob Wepfer">Johann Jacob Wepfer</a> (1620–1695) identified the cause of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemorrhagic" title="Hemorrhagic">hemorrhagic</a> stroke when he suggested that people who had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Died" title="Died">died</a> of apoplexy had bleeding in their brains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NINDS1999_46-5"><a href="#cite_note-NINDS1999-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stroke1996-Thompson_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stroke1996-Thompson-232">[232]</a></sup>
Wepfer also identified the main <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arteries" title="Arteries">arteries</a> supplying the brain, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertebral" title="Vertebral">vertebral</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carotid" title="Carotid">carotid</a> arteries, and identified the cause of a type of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ischemic" title="Ischemic">ischemic</a> stroke known as a <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_infarction" title="Cerebral infarction">cerebral infarction</a> when he suggested that <a href="/wiki/Apoplexy" title="Apoplexy">apoplexy</a> might be caused by a blockage to those vessels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NINDS1999_46-6"><a href="#cite_note-NINDS1999-46">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Virchow" title="Rudolf Virchow">Rudolf Virchow</a> first described the mechanism of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thromboembolism" title="Thromboembolism">thromboembolism</a> as a major factor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid4914683_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid4914683-237">[237]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term <i>cerebrovascular accident</i> was introduced in 1927, reflecting a "growing awareness and acceptance of vascular theories and (...) recognition of the consequences of a sudden disruption in the vascular supply of the brain".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FingerBoller2010_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-FingerBoller2010-238">[238]</a></sup> Its use is now discouraged by a number of neurology textbooks, reasoning that the connotation of fortuitousness carried by the word <i>accident</i> insufficiently highlights the modifiability of the underlying risk factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scadding2011_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scadding2011-239">[239]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SirvenMalamut2008_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-SirvenMalamut2008-240">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KaufmanMilstein2012_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-KaufmanMilstein2012-241">[241]</a></sup> <i>Cerebrovascular insult</i> may be used interchangeably.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mosby_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mosby-242">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term <i>brain attack</i> was introduced for use to underline the acute nature of stroke according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Stroke_Association" title="American Stroke Association">American Stroke Association</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mosby_242-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mosby-242">[242]</a></sup> which has used the term since 1990,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSA_Brain_Attack_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-NSA_Brain_Attack-243">[243]</a></sup> and is used colloquially to refer to both ischemic as well as hemorrhagic stroke.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span></h2>
<p>As of 2017, <a href="/wiki/Angioplasty" title="Angioplasty">angioplasty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stent" title="Stent">stents</a> were under preliminary <a href="/wiki/Clinical_research" title="Clinical research">clinical research</a> to determine the possible therapeutic advantages of these procedures in comparison to therapy with <a href="/wiki/Statin" title="Statin">statins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antithrombotic" title="Antithrombotic">antithrombotics</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Antihypertensive_drug" title="Antihypertensive drug">antihypertensive drugs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morris-245">[245]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
